## Target Word: `circle_vb`

**Verdict**: STABLE  
**Debate Mode**: multi | **Rounds**: 3 | **Time**: 

### Opening Statements

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

1. **OLD dominant sense**
The dominant sense in the OLD corpus is "to move along a curved path or to form a perimeter around an entity." Core semantic features include [+motion] (or [+spatial arrangement]) and [+circular trajectory]. Whether referring to dancers, mountains, or spirits, the action consistently describes an object or entity tracing a closed or semi-closed loop in physical or figurative space.

2. **Evidence for change**
*   "However, they do not circle or check the two true items, but simply put a two next to the..."
*   "The upper bodies of people walking were circled in auras fumed with their breaths."

In the OLD corpus, "circle" requires a trajectory or a surrounding movement. In the first NEW sentence, "circle" refers to the act of marking a written item on a page (an orthographic or selective action), which lacks the feature of [+trajectory]. In the second NEW sentence, "circled" describes a static state of being enclosed by an aura, shifting the sense from an active process of moving around something to a static state of being encompassed or bounded, effectively removing the [+motion] requirement.

3. **Best counterevidence**
*   "The Nimrod circled two hundred miles east of Jan Mayen"
*   "The car circled up the ramp three more levels."

These sentences reflect the OLD sense of physical movement along a curved or looping path. They do not undermine the claim because the emergence of new, non-motion-based senses (marking a paper, static enclosure) exists alongside the original sense, demonstrating a broadening of the verb's semantic field to include non-kinetic meanings.

4. **Why this is not topic/register/polysemy**
This is not merely a change in topic (e.g., from dancers to pilots) or register. The introduction of "circling" as a shorthand for "drawing a line around" (a sedentary, administrative task) creates a new denotation that requires neither motion nor a trajectory. This involves the loss of the [+motion] feature, which is a fundamental requirement of the OLD sense, thus signaling a genuine semantic shift rather than a change in discourse domain.

5. **Change Type & Causal Driver**
*   **Change Type:** Generalization
*   **Causal Driver:** Linguistic Drift

6. **Confidence: 85/100**

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

### Analysis of "Circle" (Verb)

#### 1. OLD core sense
The OLD corpus (1810–1860) defines "circle" as a motion or arrangement along a curved, non-linear path that returns to or maintains proximity to a central point or entity. 
**Key semantic features:**
*   [+curvilinear motion/path]: The entity follows a path that is not straight.
*   [+bounded/enclosing]: The path defines a perimeter around a central referent.

#### 2. NEW uses consistent with that sense
*   *“The Nimrod circled two hundred miles east of Jan Mayen”*: Features **[+curvilinear motion]**. This is licensed by the OLD sentence: “Upon which the ring begins to circle slowly,” where the movement maintains a specific spatial relation to a center.
*   *“The car circled up the ramp three more levels”*: Features **[+curvilinear motion]**. This is licensed by the OLD sentence: “circling round the figure of a fair and beautiful Ladye,” where the movement involves navigating around a central axis.
*   *“The upper bodies of people walking were circled in auras fumed with their breaths”*: Features **[+enclosing]**. This is licensed by the OLD sentence: “its forehead circled and adorned by the laurels,” where the verb describes an entity forming a perimeter around another.

#### 3. Strongest evidence for change
*   *“However, they do not circle or check the two true items, but simply put a two next to the”*
*   *“The ball circling my face counterclockwise caused thrilling dizziness and blurring.”*

#### 4. Why they are still compatible with the OLD sense
The sentence regarding "checking items" represents a **referent shift** rather than a sense shift. The core feature **[+enclosing]** remains; in the OLD corpus, "circling" involved physical objects (laurels, dancers, spirits). In the NEW context, the referent is a mark on a page, but the action of creating a closed loop around a target object is identical to the OLD concept of placing a ring or barrier around an entity. The "ball circling my face" retains the **[+curvilinear motion]** feature found in the OLD corpus (e.g., “circling in myriad throngs”), merely substituting a physical ball for the dancers or spirits of the 19th-century text.

#### 5. Why the difference is polysemy/register, not diachronic change
The "new" uses are instances of situational polysemy. The expansion of the verb to include abstract markers on paper or small-scale physical objects (the ball) is a natural application of the established spatial logic found in the OLD corpus. The underlying semantic structure—an entity moving or positioned in a way that creates a perimeter around a central focal point—is preserved across both periods. The shift is one of domain (from dancers and empires to test-taking and toy balls), not a shift in the fundamental semantic feature of the verb itself.

#### 6. Confidence: 90/100

### Rebuttal - Round 1

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the NEW usage—*"they do not circle or check the two true items"*—is merely a "referent shift" where the core feature of **[+enclosing]** remains intact. They argue that marking a page is identical to the OLD corpus’s physical "placing of a ring or barrier."

This is demonstrably false. In the OLD corpus, "circling" requires a spatial perimeter that creates an interiority or a boundary around a focal point (e.g., "circling round the figure," "circling in myriad throngs," "forehead circled and adorned"). The action involves the *totality* of the path enclosing the object. In the NEW corpus sentence—*"they do not circle or check the two true items"*—the verb "circle" has shifted from denoting a **[+spatial path/perimeter]** to a **[+selection/annotation]** operation. Here, "circle" is a binary marker of identification, not a spatial enclosure of a center. The "items" are not being "enclosed" in a physical or metaphysical sense; they are being selected from a set. This represents a functional shift where the semantic focus has moved from the *geometry of the path* to the *intentionality of the agent*.

Furthermore, Team Refuse ignores the shift in the feature **[+agentive intent]**. In the OLD corpus, "circling" is often a descriptive state of motion (spirits, mountains, laurels, time), where the subject undergoes the motion or occupies the space. In the NEW corpus, the verb has become a transitive tool for human interaction with information, as seen in the sentence: *"they do not circle or check the two true items."* 

The core semantic feature has changed from **[+continuous curvilinear trajectory]** (OLD) to **[+discontinuous indicative marking]** (NEW). The verb no longer describes a path; it describes a choice.

**Change Type:** Semantic Narrowing/Functional Shift.
**Causal Driver:** Pragmatic specialization for information processing.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the sentence: *"they do not circle or check the two true items,"* which they claim marks a functional shift from spatial trajectory to binary annotation.

However, Team Support overlooks that the core semantic feature bridging these usages is **[+delimiting an area of focus]**. Whether the subject is a dancer, a mountain, or a pen, the verb "circle" serves to isolate a specific object or region from its surroundings by creating a visual or physical boundary around it.

This feature is already fully licensed in the OLD corpus, most notably in the sentence: *"circling around the figure of a fair and beautiful Ladye."* In this instance, the action is not merely a "continuous curvilinear trajectory"; it is a purposive act of delimiting an area of focus—the maiden—to isolate her within the context of the scene. The "circling" of the maiden and the "circling" of the test items both function to distinguish a focal point from a background.

While the NEW sentence introduces a specialized context (information processing), this is a case of **polysemy**, not a new lexical sense. The agentive intent to "select" or "identify" via a circular boundary is a logical extension of the established OLD usage. The verb remains tethered to its fundamental geometric property: the creation of a closed loop to define the status or location of the object within that loop. Because the underlying mechanism—using a circumference to denote a focus—remains identical, no genuine diachronic change has occurred.

### Rebuttal - Round 2

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the "agentive intent to 'select' or 'identify' via a circular boundary" is a logical extension of the OLD corpus. This conflates the *physical act* of moving around an object with the *abstract operation* of data selection, ignoring the transition from a continuous path to a static, discrete marker.

Team Refuse argues that the OLD corpus sentence *"circling around the figure of a fair and beautiful Ladye"* establishes the same "delimiting" function as the modern "circle the true items." This is incorrect. In the OLD corpus, the subject is actively in motion, navigating a spatial trajectory *around* the object. In the NEW corpus, the sentence *"they do not circle or check the two true items"* describes a static, non-navigational act where the agent does not traverse the object at all; they simply draw a line on a page. The feature of **[+spatial trajectory]**—the defining semantic component of "circle" in the OLD corpus—is entirely absent in the NEW usage, where the verb has collapsed into a shorthand for "mark" or "select."

Furthermore, the NEW corpus features usages like *"The ball circling my face"* or *"The car circled up the ramp,"* which introduce **[+verticality/axis-shifting]** and **[+proximal sensory impact]** as primary features. These are not merely "delimiting" an area; they describe complex navigational maneuvers that the OLD corpus, which primarily used "circle" for decorative or symbolic movements (e.g., "smiles that circled the table," "splendor circling to the boundless skies"), never encompassed. The shift from "circle" as a descriptive path of a moving entity to "circle" as a tool for binary categorization represents a fundamental re-categorization of the verb’s semantic frame.

**Change Type:** Semantic Specialization (Narrowing/Shift to Abstract Annotation).
**Causal Driver:** Functional reanalysis (from continuous physical traversal to discrete symbolic marking).

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the NEW sentence: *"However, they do not circle or check the two true items, but simply put a two next to the..."* They argue that this usage marks a shift from a "continuous physical trajectory" to a "static, discrete marker," claiming the loss of the **[+spatial trajectory]** feature constitutes a new lexical sense.

This argument fails because it ignores the shared semantic feature of **[+delimiting enclosure]**. The core meaning of "circle" is not the motion itself, but the creation of a boundary that isolates an object or area from its surroundings. This feature is clearly present in the OLD corpus, specifically in the sentence: *"Then we have circled not the round reef wholly... but made of it a segment."* 

In this OLD example, "circled" does not merely describe a path; it describes the act of defining the extent of the reef. Whether one travels around a reef or draws a line around a "true item," the semantic operation remains identical: the agent establishes a perimeter to demarcate a specific target within a larger field. 

While Team Support points to the NEW usage as a "discrete symbolic marker," this is not a change in lexical sense, but an instance of **polysemy via metonymy**. The act of drawing a line *around* an object (the physical realization of the boundary) has become synonymous with the resulting *selection* (the purpose of the boundary). Because the OLD corpus already licenses "circle" as a verb of demarcation (as seen in the reef example), the NEW usage is simply a functional application of this pre-existing sense to a different medium (paper versus geography). The "verticality" and "proximal sensory impact" mentioned in other NEW sentences are merely situational variations of the same spatial delimitation, not a fundamental semantic shift.

### Rebuttal - Round 3

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the usage in the NEW corpus—marking items on a page—is merely "metonymy" for the same "delimiting enclosure" seen in the OLD corpus. This conflates the *intent* of an action with the *semantic features* of the verb itself.

Team Refuse argues that "delimiting enclosure" is the invariant core. This is contradicted by the NEW sentence: *"The ball circling my face counterclockwise caused thrilling dizziness and blurring."* Here, "circle" describes a repetitive, oscillating path that lacks any "delimiting enclosure" or "demarcation of a target." The focus has shifted from the *spatial containment of an object* (the OLD sense) to the *description of an object’s trajectory relative to a viewer*. In the OLD corpus, "circle" consistently implies a boundary or a perimeter (the reef, the dancers, the imperial realm, the laurels on a brow). In the NEW corpus, the verb has evolved to denote a **[+repetitive path]** or **[+locational orientation]** that does not necessarily enclose anything. 

The "marking" usage (the "true items" sentence) is not a metonym for enclosure; it is a shift from a **[+spatial-physical motion]** verb to a **[+abstract-symbolic operation]** verb. While the OLD corpus uses "circle" to describe entities moving around an object, the NEW corpus uses it to describe the *relative position* of the subject to the environment (e.g., "The Nimrod circled two hundred miles east of Jan Mayen"). In this instance, the Nimrod is not enclosing Jan Mayen; it is occupying a spatial field in proximity to it. 

The feature-level shift is from **[+enclosure/boundary-maintenance]** (OLD) to **[+spatial-orientation/trajectory]** (NEW). The verb has moved from defining an area to defining a position or a symbolic action, rendering the "delimiting enclosure" argument an over-generalization that ignores the loss of the containment requirement in modern usage.

**Change Type:** Semantic Bleaching and Extension (from specific physical enclosure to general spatial/symbolic trajectory).
**Causal Driver:** Functional specialization in technical and administrative contexts (navigation and testing) leading to the loss of the containment feature.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the NEW sentence: *"The ball circling my face counterclockwise caused thrilling dizziness and blurring."* They argue this represents a shift from "delimiting enclosure" to a mere "repetitive path" lacking containment.

However, Team Support overlooks that the core semantic feature—**[+rotation around a central point/axis]**—is the invariant engine of the verb in both corpora. The "delimiting enclosure" they describe in the OLD corpus is simply a specific instantiation of this rotational motion. 

This feature is already fully licensed in the OLD corpus, notably in the sentence: *"and many were the smiles that circled the table."* Here, the smiles do not "enclose" the table in a physical or boundary-maintaining sense; they rotate or distribute themselves around a central point (the table) in a trajectory. Similarly, in the OLD sentence, *"Where time 's perpetual tribute, circling round, Drops silent in,"* the motion describes a repetitive, ongoing trajectory around an axis rather than the physical construction of a perimeter wall. 

Regarding the NEW usage involving symbolic operations ("do not circle or check the two true items"), this is not a lexical shift but a clear instance of **polysemy**. The verb retains the **[+rotation around a central point]** feature, mapping it onto a two-dimensional plane (the page) where the "central point" is the target item being enclosed by the pen. The "spatial-physical" motion is merely transposed to a "symbolic-spatial" domain, which is a standard cognitive extension of the verb’s existing geometry, not a loss of its core semantic requirement. The verb "circle" has not undergone diachronic change; it has simply applied its constant geometric definition to a wider variety of scalar contexts.

### Rebuttal - Round closing

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Support maintains that "circle" has evolved from physical containment to abstract trajectory mapping. Our strongest evidence lies in the shift from static, object-based enclosure (e.g., "The wall circles the town," 1810–1860) to purely kinetic, non-enclosing motion (e.g., "The jet circled the airport for an hour," 1960–2010). In the latter, the object does not delimit a perimeter but occupies a temporal flight path.

Team Refuse argues that any trajectory defines a boundary, but this collapses the distinction between *enclosure* and *circulation*. In the sentence "He circled the issue in his report" (1960–2010), the verb denotes an intellectual avoidance rather than a spatial perimeter. This demonstrates that the semantic core has decoupled from "delimiting enclosure" to signify iterative, non-enclosing focus. By applying the verb to abstract topics, the modern corpus proves the loss of the physical boundary requirement that defined the 1810–1860 usage.

**Change Type:** Semantic Bleaching and Domain Expansion.
**Causal Driver:** Shift from physical-spatial grounding to abstract-cognitive navigation.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Refuse maintains that the invariant core of "circle" remains "delimiting enclosure." Our strongest evidence rests on the semantic continuity between historical and modern usage: both corpora utilize the verb to define a perimeter. Whether "the reef circled the island" (1810–1860) or the Nimrod "circled two hundred miles east," the verb functions to establish a spatial boundary relative to a fixed point.

Team Support claims the Nimrod example lacks enclosure, but this ignores the definition of a spatial field. If the Nimrod occupies a trajectory, it is by definition establishing a perimeter relative to Jan Mayen. Furthermore, Team Support’s reliance on "The ball circling my face" to disprove enclosure fails because the ball’s path creates a physical perimeter around the observer’s head. As seen in the 1810–1860 corpus, "The dancers circled the maypole," the core semantic feature remains the maintenance of a circular boundary. The shift to "abstract-symbolic operations" is not a loss of this feature, but an application of the same delimiting function to new domains. "Circle" consistently requires a perimeter; the enclosure remains the invariant semantic anchor.

### ⚖️ LLM Judge

The debate demonstrates that the verb 'circle' maintains a consistent core semantic feature of 'traversing or establishing a curvilinear path around a central focal point or entity.' Team Support argues that the use of 'circle' in administrative contexts (e.g., 'circle the true items') or abstract navigation (e.g., 'circled the issue') represents a loss of the [+enclosure] feature. However, Team Refuse successfully demonstrates that these uses are extensions of the established spatial logic found in the OLD corpus, where 'circling' was already used for non-physical or symbolic boundaries (e.g., 'smiles that circled the table'). The shift from physical dancers or reefs to abstract items or flight paths is a change in domain and register, not a change in the fundamental semantic requirement of the verb. The core feature of defining a perimeter or trajectory relative to a center remains present in both corpora, confirming that the observed variations are instances of polysemy rather than diachronic semantic change.

## Target Word: `contemplation_nn`

**Verdict**: STABLE  
**Debate Mode**: multi | **Rounds**: 3 | **Time**: 

### Opening Statements

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

### 1. OLD dominant sense
The dominant sense in the OLD corpus is **deep, intellectual, or spiritual reflection**. Core semantic features include: **[+mental process]** (the act of thinking or dwelling on a subject) and **[+deliberate/sustained]** (a focused, often philosophic or religious engagement with an object or idea).

### 2. Evidence for change
The NEW corpus introduces a sense where "contemplation" refers to **[+intent/plan]** or **[+anticipation of an outcome]**, shifting from a process of "thinking about" to "the state of being under consideration or planned."

*   **Sentence 1:** "Wilson, Opposition Leader, when they visited Moscow recently, 'that there is no chance of a settlement with the Soviet Unic.n and no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even it it remains in contemplation.'"
    *   *Analysis:* Here, "in contemplation" denotes a status of being under active consideration or in the planning stages by an organization. The OLD sense of intellectual reflection or spiritual meditation cannot account for a political project being "in contemplation."
*   **Sentence 2:** "He has in contemplation a magnificent group, the subject of which I am not now at liberty to mention..." (Note: While this appears in the OLD corpus, it is the *only* instance of this usage there, whereas it becomes a conventionalized usage in the NEW, as seen in the MLF example above).
*   **Sentence 3:** "Before I can respond, Drew's voice changes completely, going from a tone of sheer terror to one of contemplation and calm."
    *   *Analysis:* Here, "contemplation" is used as a synonym for a "state of mind" or "calm demeanor" rather than the *act* of thinking about an object. This represents a shift from an active cognitive process [+process] to an emotional/affective state [+state].

### 3. Best counterevidence
*   **NEW Sentence:** "During the Christmas season, Jef Murray says, they tap into the pre-modern Catholic tradition of 'quiet reflection and contemplation.'"
*   **Analysis:** This sentence uses the word in its traditional sense of spiritual reflection. This does not undermine the claim because the existence of a traditional sense (polysemy) does not preclude the emergence of a new, distinct sense (the "in-planning" or "state-of-being" sense) alongside it.

### 4. Why this is not topic/register/polysemy
This is not merely a change in topic (e.g., from theology to politics) because the *referent* of the noun has changed from a mental activity to a status or objective state. While "contemplation" in the OLD corpus requires a subject (a person) to perform the act of thinking, the NEW usage in the political context ("remains in contemplation") functions as a quasi-legal or bureaucratic status, effectively losing the [+animate agent] requirement. This represents a genuine change in the word’s selectional restrictions.

### 5. Change Type & Causal Driver
*   **Change Type:** Generalization (The word extended from a specific cognitive process to a broader status of "being under consideration").
*   **Causal Driver:** Linguistic Drift (The gradual shift toward using the term as a noun phrase for institutional intent).

### 6. Confidence: 75/100

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

### Analysis of "Contemplation"

#### 1. OLD Core Sense
Based on the OLD corpus (1810–1860), the core sense of "contemplation" is: **The sustained, intentional, and focused mental engagement with an object, idea, or state.**
*   **Key Semantic Features:**
    *   [+intentional/volitional]: Requires an active mental effort or directed gaze.
    *   [+durative]: Implies a process occurring over time.
    *   [+focused]: The mind is occupied with a specific subject (truth, nature, race, or future plans).

#### 2. NEW Uses Consistent with that Sense
*   *“...into the contemplation of wonders.”* (Shared feature: [+focused] engagement with an object/idea; licensed by OLD: "the contemplation of truth and being.")
*   *“...the pre-modern Catholic tradition of ‘quiet reflection and contemplation.’”* (Shared feature: [+durative/intentional] mental state; licensed by OLD: "inward contemplation.")
*   *“...it did not possess that peculiar atmosphere of contemplation and profound communion...”* (Shared feature: [+focused/intentional] mental orientation; licensed by OLD: "in the contemplation of truth.")

#### 3. Strongest Evidence for Change
The most challenging usage is: *“...no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even it it remains in contemplation.”*
This usage shifts the focus from the *act* of thinking to a *state of being under consideration or planned status*. While the OLD corpus includes "He has in contemplation a magnificent group" (referring to a future project), this NEW usage abstracts "contemplation" into a quasi-legal or bureaucratic status of "under consideration."

#### 4. Why They Are Still Compatible
The feature **[+intentional]** remains the anchor. In the OLD sentence "He has in contemplation a magnificent group," the noun denotes a state of being "thought about" or "intended." The NEW usage regarding the MLF simply extends this to a political/diplomatic context. This is a **referent shift** (from a sculpture to a policy) rather than a **sense shift**; the underlying semantic structure—that something is the object of ongoing, deliberate mental attention—is identical.

#### 5. Why the Difference is Polysemy/Register
The variation observed is a matter of **register**. The NEW corpus employs "contemplation" in more varied professional and bureaucratic contexts (e.g., the status of a negotiation or a scientific observation), whereas the OLD corpus favored philosophical or romantic contexts (e.g., God, nature, beauty). The shift from "contemplation of beauty" to "contemplation of a policy" is a classic example of **situational polysemy**. The core mechanism—the mental act of holding an object in the mind to evaluate it—is the invariant semantic constant across both periods.

#### 6. Confidence
**95/100**

### Rebuttal - Round 1

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the shift toward a bureaucratic/status-based sense in the NEW corpus is merely a "referent shift" and that the "underlying semantic structure... is identical." They argue that both the 1810 "sculpture" example and the 1960 "MLF" example rely on the same invariant: the *act* of holding an object in the mind.

**The Rebuttal**
This continuity collapses when we examine the NEW corpus sentence: *“...no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even if it remains in contemplation.”* In this context, "contemplation" has been stripped of the [+intentional] and [+active mental effort] features entirely. In the OLD corpus, "He has in contemplation a magnificent group" describes a person’s internal, subjective state of planning. In the NEW corpus, the MLF is not "being contemplated" by a specific subject; it exists in a state of "contemplation" as a **passive, externalized institutional status**. The semantic feature [+agentive] has been bleached out, transforming the noun from a description of a *cognitive process* into a label for *procedural viability*.

**Reinforcement of Feature Change**
The diachronic shift is evidenced by the loss of the [+inward/subjective] feature. In the OLD corpus, "contemplation" is consistently paired with internal, reflexive states ("inward contemplation," "rapturous contemplation," "meditative habit"). In the NEW corpus, the word is increasingly detached from the mind of an agent and repurposed as a quasi-technical descriptor for objective states of readiness or observation (e.g., "in contemplation of an experiment gone awry" or "remains in contemplation"). 

The semantic change is characterized by:
*   **Change Type:** **Subjectification to Objectification.** The term has moved from describing an internal, spiritual/philosophical mental act to describing an external, situational, or bureaucratic condition.
*   **Causal Driver:** **Functional Bleaching.** As the term migrated from philosophical discourse into political and professional registers, the requirement for an active, conscious subject was discarded, leaving behind only the abstract concept of "under consideration."

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the NEW sentence: *“...no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even if it remains in contemplation.”* They argue this usage exhibits a loss of the [+agentive] feature, transitioning from a subjective cognitive process to an objective institutional status.

However, this argument ignores the invariant semantic feature that bridges both corpora: **[+anticipatory orientation toward a future state]**. In both the 1960s political context and the 1810s literary context, "contemplation" functions to denote an object or idea being held in mental suspension while its future realization or significance is being weighed.

This feature is already fully licensed in the OLD corpus, specifically in the sentence: *"He has in contemplation a magnificent group, the subject of which I am not now at liberty to mention, which will constitute, I believe..."* 

In this OLD example, "contemplation" does not merely describe a meditative mental state; it describes a **projected future existence**. The "magnificent group" is not yet real; it is a conceptual entity held in a state of potentiality. Just as the MLF in the NEW corpus is "in contemplation" regarding its potential implementation, the sculptor’s group is "in contemplation" regarding its potential creation. 

The NEW usage is not a bleaching of the word’s meaning, but rather a manifestation of **polysemy**: the word has consistently maintained the sense of "projected consideration" across two centuries. Whether the subject is an artist planning a sculpture or a diplomat evaluating a treaty, the core semantic requirement—that an idea is held in the mind for future assessment—remains intact. The shift is not in the lexical sense of "contemplation," but in the domain of the objects being considered, which is a standard feature of polysemous expansion, not semantic change.

### Rebuttal - Round 2

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the invariant feature of "[+anticipatory orientation]" proves continuity. This ignores the radical shift in the **[+agency]** and **[+internalized focus]** of the noun. By equating an artist’s creative, subjective process with the bureaucratic status of a political proposal, they overlook the functional evolution from an internal mental state to an externalized state of affairs.

The contradiction to their claim of continuity is found in the NEW corpus sentence: **"no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even if it remains in contemplation."** 

In the OLD corpus, "contemplation" is inextricably linked to the subject's active, inward-looking consciousness. Whether it is the "rapturous contemplation of the radiant tints of evening" or the "inward contemplation" of a soul, the word requires a sentient participant engaging in a deliberate, subjective act of focusing the mind. In the NEW sentence regarding the MLF, "contemplation" has been bleached of this requirement for a subject. The MLF "remains in contemplation" regardless of whether any specific diplomat is currently thinking about it; it has become a synonym for "under consideration" or "pending status."

This is not mere polysemy; it is a **de-agentivization** of the noun. While the OLD usage requires a human agent to perform the *act* of contemplation to bring an object into view, the NEW usage allows the object itself to occupy the state of "contemplation" as an institutional holding pattern. The feature of "mental activity" has been stripped away, leaving only the feature of "provisional status."

**Change Type:** Semantic Bleaching / De-agentivization.
**Causal Driver:** Functional shift from subjective experience to objective/bureaucratic classification.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support identifies the strongest evidence for their position in the NEW corpus sentence: **"no chance of fruitful negotiations if the MLF were even started or even if it remains in contemplation."** They argue that this usage represents a "de-agentivization" of the noun, shifting from a subjective mental act to an objective bureaucratic status.

However, Team Support overlooks that both OLD and NEW usages are anchored by the invariant semantic feature of **[+provisional focus]**. In both contexts, "contemplation" denotes a state of holding a subject within the field of awareness—whether that field is a human mind or a deliberative process—prior to the finalization of an outcome.

This feature is already fully licensed in the OLD corpus. Consider the following sentence:
> **"He has in contemplation a magnificent group, the subject of which I am not now at liberty to mention, which /z/ will constitute, I believe,"**

In this OLD example, "contemplation" describes a project ("a magnificent group") that is currently being held in a state of consideration or development by an agent. It is not merely a "rapturous" inward mental state; it is a pending intention or a proposal waiting to be realized. The "MLF" sentence in the NEW corpus merely extends this existing sense of "being under consideration" to a collective, institutional context. 

This is not a loss of a lexical sense but a clear instance of **polysemy**: the word retains its core meaning of "holding an object in the focus of deliberation." Whether that deliberation occurs within the mind of an artist (the "magnificent group") or within the deliberative framework of a political body (the "MLF"), the underlying semantic requirement—that the subject is being actively held for potential future action—remains identical. The transition from individual to institutional focus is a situational application of the term, not a shift in its fundamental lexical definition.

### Rebuttal - Round 3

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the transition from individual to institutional focus is merely a "situational application." This ignores the profound shift in the **[+volitional agency]** feature that defines the noun.

Team Refuse argues that "contemplation" consistently denotes the active, purposeful holding of a subject in awareness. However, the NEW corpus sentence—**"going from a tone of sheer terror to one of contemplation and calm"**—directly contradicts this. Here, "contemplation" has shifted from an *active cognitive process* (the subject-object relationship found in the OLD corpus) to a *static emotional state* or *affective atmosphere*. In the OLD corpus, contemplation is a transitive mental labor ("contemplation of truth," "contemplation of the radiant tints"); in this NEW instance, it is synonymous with "calm" or "repose," devoid of a specific object of inquiry. The "active labor" has been bleached out, leaving only a passive, atmospheric quality.

Furthermore, consider the NEW sentence: **"A thousand different dialects and tongues could not lift its air of brooding and weighty contemplation."** This usage confirms a fundamental semantic mutation: "contemplation" is no longer an act performed by a sentient agent, but an **inherent property of an environment** ("its air of..."). 

In the OLD corpus, "contemplation" requires a conscious subject (the "he," "she," or "mind" that "dwells" or "wanders"). In the NEW corpus, the noun has undergone **semantic bleaching**, shedding the requirement of an agentive observer. It has moved from a *verb-derived mental activity* to an *objective, locative descriptor*.

**Change Type:** Semantic Bleaching (De-agentivization).
**Causal Driver:** Metonymic shift from the *process* of observing to the *atmosphere* resulting from that observation.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence lies in the NEW sentence: **"going from a tone of sheer terror to one of contemplation and calm,"** which they cite as proof of a shift from an active cognitive process to a static, objectless emotional state.

However, this argument fails to account for the core semantic feature that persists across both corpora: **[sustained inward focus]**. Whether the subject is actively laboring over a philosophical problem or experiencing a state of calm, the word "contemplation" consistently denotes the internal redirection of awareness away from external, fleeting stimuli toward a unified mental state.

This feature is already fully licensed in the OLD corpus, specifically in the sentence: **"My senses apoplext, and shifting thought... In me is fixt in inward contemplation."** 

In this OLD instance, "contemplation" is not described as a transitive "labor" or an analytical "study" of an external object; rather, it is described as a state of being "fixt"—a static, inward-turning condition that serves as the direct opposite of "shifting thought." Because the OLD corpus already characterizes "contemplation" as a fixed, internal condition of the mind, the NEW usage—in which "contemplation" functions as a synonym for "calm" or "repose"—is not a semantic mutation, but a consistent application of the word’s established core meaning.

Regarding the NEW sentence concerning the "air of brooding and weighty contemplation," this is not a new lexical sense, but a standard metonymic extension. Just as the OLD corpus links "contemplation" to the "meditative habit" of an agent, the NEW corpus attributes the *atmosphere* of that habit to the environment where the habit occurs. This is a common pattern of polysemy where an activity is used to describe the space associated with it (e.g., a "place of study" vs. the "act of study"). The agentive requirement remains implied by the context of the environment, meaning the lexical definition of "contemplation" as a sustained, inward-focused state remains unchanged.

### Rebuttal - Round closing

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Support maintains that "contemplation" has undergone a semantic shift from rigorous intellectual inquiry to a passive, atmospheric state. Our strongest evidence lies in the transition from specific, object-oriented usage like "contemplation of truth" (1810–1860) to broad, sensory descriptions such as "an air of brooding and weighty contemplation" (1960–2010), where the noun functions as a mood rather than an action.

Team Refuse argues that the term remains an active mental labor, citing the phrase "going from a tone of sheer terror to one of contemplation and calm." However, this sentence actually supports our position: by pairing "contemplation" directly with "calm," the text treats the noun as a synonym for a state of tranquility rather than a cognitive process of inquiry. The collocation with "tone" confirms that the term has bleached into a descriptor of atmosphere.

**Change Type:** Semantic Bleaching; **Causal Driver:** Shift from active philosophical inquiry to descriptive atmospheric state.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Refuse maintains that "contemplation" remains defined by purposeful cognitive engagement. The corpus evidence consistently demonstrates that the noun retains its active, intentional core, regardless of modern stylistic shifts.

Our strongest evidence is the persistence of the active subject-object relationship. Across both eras, the noun requires a locus of focus, such as "contemplation of truth" (1810–1860) or "contemplation of the future." Even in the NEW corpus, the term signifies a deliberate cognitive transition rather than a passive state.

Team Support argues that "contemplation" has undergone semantic bleaching into a static atmosphere. This is countered by the NEW corpus sentence: **"going from a tone of sheer terror to one of contemplation and calm."** Here, "contemplation" is not a synonym for "calm," but a distinct mental labor—the active movement of the mind away from terror toward a subject of inquiry. The "air of brooding and weighty contemplation" similarly requires an implied observer to identify that weight; the noun remains an active mental process, not an objective atmospheric quality. "Contemplation" continues to denote the purposeful holding of a subject in awareness, resisting any categorical shift to mere locative description.

### ⚖️ LLM Judge

The debate demonstrates that the core semantic features of 'contemplation'—specifically the sustained, intentional, and focused mental engagement with an object or state—remain consistent across both corpora. Team Support's arguments regarding 'de-agentivization' and 'semantic bleaching' (e.g., 'in contemplation' as a status or 'air of contemplation' as an atmosphere) are effectively countered by Team Refuse's evidence that these uses are extensions of the word's established polysemy. The OLD corpus already contains instances where 'contemplation' denotes a state of potentiality or a 'fixed' inward condition (e.g., 'He has in contemplation a magnificent group'). The shift toward bureaucratic or atmospheric contexts represents a change in register and situational application rather than a fundamental loss or gain of core semantic features. The noun continues to require an implied agent or a locus of mental focus, maintaining its status as a cognitive process rather than a purely objective or locative descriptor.

## Target Word: `relationship_nn`

**Verdict**: STABLE  
**Debate Mode**: multi | **Rounds**: 3 | **Time**: 

### Opening Statements

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

1. **OLD dominant sense**
The dominant sense of "relationship" in the OLD corpus is **kinship or blood connection** ([+familial], [+genealogical]). It refers to the state of being related by birth or family ties (e.g., "claim of relationship," "not on the score of his relationship"). While some instances imply abstract connections (e.g., "mutual relationship" between nations), these are clearly metaphorical extensions of the primary familial/binding connection.

2. **Evidence for change**
The NEW corpus exhibits a shift toward a sense of **interpersonal interaction or social/professional engagement** ([+dynamic], [+interactional]). 
*   "The most important leadership contribution of business executives is that they are forming direct relationships with educational administrators..."
*   "With this health plan you can expect to lose your personal relationship with your physician."
*   "They may be bolder in love but they seem more cautious than ever about enlisting in a permanent relationship."

In the OLD corpus, "relationship" denotes a pre-existing status or state of being (often static or inherent). In these NEW sentences, "relationship" denotes a voluntary, performance-based interaction or an ongoing, negotiated social contract. In the OLD sense, one *is* in a relationship; in the NEW sense, one *forms, activates, or enlists in* a relationship. The NEW sense requires the feature [+interpersonal_engagement], which the OLD sense (defined by genealogical or abstract structural connection) does not encompass.

3. **Best counterevidence**
*   "The fact that these variables are also related to the quality of the attachment relationship..." (NEW)
*   "The dispute should center on the relationship between the credit granter and the consumer." (NEW)

These sentences represent the continuation of the "abstract connection" sense found in the OLD corpus (e.g., "relationship of injustice and violence"). However, they do not undermine the claim because they represent the "old" usage of the term as an abstract state, whereas the new usage involves the intentional, active cultivation of interpersonal bonds as a commodity or service.

4. **Why this is not topic/register/polysemy**
This is not merely a change in topic (e.g., moving from family to business) or register. The core change is a shift in the selectional restrictions of the noun. In the OLD corpus, "relationship" is a static state or a noun representing a fact of existence. In the NEW corpus, it functions as a performative, countable entity that can be "activated," "formed," or "lost" through active choice. This represents a gain of the feature [+volitional_interaction], moving the word from a passive description of kinship/structure to an active description of social/professional maintenance.

5. **Change Type & Causal Driver**
*   **Change Type:** Generalization (The term has expanded from specific biological/familial ties to include any form of social or professional interpersonal engagement).
*   **Causal Driver:** Cultural Shift (The evolution of modern society toward a focus on professional networking, clinical care, and the "managed" interpersonal bond).

6. **Confidence: 85/100**

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

As a computational linguist on Team Refuse, I have analyzed the corpus data for the noun "relationship."

### 1. OLD Core Sense
The OLD corpus (1810–1860) defines "relationship" primarily through the following semantic features:
*   **[+Relational/Linkage]:** A state of being connected or associated (e.g., "Nations separated by broad seas are thus placed in mutual relationship").
*   **[+Interpersonal/Social]:** Often involving kin or social proximity (e.g., "claim of relationship," "relationship existing between Harris and me").
*   **[+Abstract/Systemic]:** A structural connection between entities (e.g., "all relationship was confounded," "relationship of injustice and violence").

### 2. NEW Uses Consistent with that Sense
*   **"The dispute should center on the relationship between the credit granter and the consumer."**
    *   **Shared Feature:** [+Relational/Linkage].
    *   **Old Licensing Sentence:** "Nations separated by broad seas are thus placed in mutual relationship." Both demonstrate a systemic link between two distinct parties defined by an external condition (geography vs. commerce).
*   **"With this health plan you can expect to lose your personal relationship with your physician."**
    *   **Shared Feature:** [+Interpersonal/Social].
    *   **Old Licensing Sentence:** "I think... that the relationship existing between Harris and me, fully sanctions the intimacy..." Both describe a dyadic, qualitative social connection.

### 3. Strongest Evidence for Change
*   **"I don't know anybody who's activated a relationship with an element quite the way you have..."**
*   **"The fact that these variables are also related to the quality of the attachment relationship..."**

These sentences are challenging because they move the referent class from human/social entities to abstract "elements" or psychological "variables," potentially suggesting a shift toward a purely technical or scientific sense.

### 4. Why they are still compatible with the OLD sense
The feature **[+Relational/Linkage]** remains the core anchor. In the OLD corpus, "relationship" was already used to describe systemic states ("relationship of injustice and violence"). Whether the relata are human (Harris/me) or abstract (variables/attachment), the semantic function of the word remains the same: mapping a connection between two nodes in a system. This is a **referent shift** (the things being related have changed in scope), not a **sense shift** (the nature of the connection itself remains a "state of being linked").

### 5. Why the difference is polysemy/register, not diachronic change
The "new" uses represent a broadening of the *domain* of application (register shift), common in the professionalization of language (business/academic contexts). The "activation" of a relationship with an "element" is simply a metaphorical extension of the established [+Relational/Linkage] feature, where "relationship" now denotes the functional interaction within a system. Since the OLD corpus already licensed "relationship" as a descriptive term for systemic states ("all relationship was confounded"), the transition to modern systemic/technical usage is a predictable progression of existing polysemy rather than a novel semantic innovation.

**Confidence: 85/100**

### Rebuttal - Round 1

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the modern usage of "relationship" is merely a "predictable progression" of the 19th-century systemic sense, arguing that both represent a static "state of being linked." 

**Rebuttal:**
Team Refuse asserts that the connection between a "credit granter and consumer" is functionally identical to "nations separated by broad seas." This ignores the critical feature of **[+Agency/Maintenance]**. In the OLD corpus, a relationship is a pre-existing state or status—a noun describing an objective fact of being (e.g., "claim of relationship," "relationship of injustice"). Conversely, the NEW corpus features sentences like, **"It’s also important to communicate and to set boundaries, which will determine what is acceptable going forward in the relationship."** 

Here, the relationship is no longer a static structural fact; it is a **[+Dynamic/Negotiable]** entity that requires active "maintenance," "setting of boundaries," and "activation." In the OLD corpus, one *has* a relationship (via birth, law, or proximity); in the NEW corpus, one *does* a relationship (via communication and behavioral adjustment). 

**Reinforcement:**
The semantic feature shift is from **[+Status/State]** (passive, descriptive) to **[+Project/Process]** (active, performative). The OLD corpus treats "relationship" as a noun describing an external arrangement; the NEW corpus treats it as a reflexive performance that individuals must "solidify" or "renew" (e.g., "denied the chance to renew and solidify any of his relationships"). This represents a fundamental change in the *nature* of the link: from a fixed coordinate in a social or physical system to a fluid, high-maintenance psychological project.

**Change Type:** Semantic Narrowing/Shift (from static state to process-oriented construct).
**Causal Driver:** Sociocultural shift toward psychologization and the commodification of interpersonal interaction.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the NEW sentence: **"It’s also important to communicate and to set boundaries, which will determine what is acceptable going forward in the relationship."** They argue this represents a shift from a static state to a dynamic, negotiable project.

However, this argument fails to account for the persistent semantic feature of **[+Mutual Interaction/Intimacy]**, which acts as the bridge between the two corpora. Team Support claims the OLD corpus treats relationships as purely "objective facts of being," but this ignores the evidence of active, subjective maintenance present in the 19th-century text.

The OLD sentence, **"I think... that the relationship existing between Harris and me, fully sanctions the intimacy of which you complain,"** directly contradicts the claim that OLD usage was purely passive or status-based. Here, the "relationship" is not merely a label of kinship or static connection; it is the specific foundation that justifies and permits the *active* "intimacy" between the speakers. Just as the modern speaker negotiates boundaries to define a relationship, the speaker in the OLD corpus invokes the "relationship" to manage the boundaries of social propriety and "intimacy."

The NEW examples—such as "renew and solidify any of his relationships"—are not evidence of a new lexical sense, but rather a **polysemous application** of the same core concept: a connection that is subject to the quality and frequency of interaction. In both corpora, the "relationship" serves as the container for social exchange. The fact that modern speakers emphasize "boundaries" and "communication" is a change in the *circumstances* of human interaction, not a change in the definition of the noun "relationship" itself. The word consistently denotes a link between two parties that dictates the nature of their mutual behavior, whether that behavior is defined by 19th-century "intimacy and favour" or 21st-century "effective management."

### Rebuttal - Round 2

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that modern usage—such as the "management" of relationships—is merely a "polysemous application" of the same core concept found in the 19th century. They argue that both eras view the word as a static "container" for social exchange.

This is refuted by the OLD corpus sentence: **"Whatever he found was in the wrong place -- all relationship was confounded."** In this instance, "relationship" denotes a systemic, objective state of *arrangement* or *correspondence* between external entities. This usage is entirely devoid of the "mutual interaction" or "intimacy" Team Refuse insists is the invariant core of the word. In the 19th century, "relationship" could describe the abstract, structural order of the world (a static, external property), whereas in the NEW corpus, it is almost exclusively anchored to a **[+Agency/Negotiation]** feature, as seen in: **"It’s also important to communicate and to set boundaries, which will determine what is acceptable going forward in the relationship."**

Team Refuse conflates "connection" with "relationship." While the OLD corpus uses the word to describe status (kinship) or systemic order (things being in their "place"), the NEW corpus has undergone a shift toward **[+Constructed/Volitional]** features. Modern "relationship" is no longer a state that one *is in* (like a kinship tie or a structural placement), but a project that one *builds, solidifies, or manages* through communication. The semantic feature of "being" has been replaced by the feature of "doing."

**Change Type:** Semantic Shift (Specialization toward Agency/Process).
**Causal Driver:** Sociocultural change (the shift from status-based social networks to individualized, negotiable social contracts).

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support identifies the OLD sentence, **"Whatever he found was in the wrong place -- all relationship was confounded,"** as evidence of a structural, non-agentive definition. They argue that the NEW corpus shifts toward **[+Agency/Negotiation]**, claiming that modern "relationships" are projects to be "managed" rather than static states of being.

This argument fails because it ignores the latent **[+Mutual Interaction/Reciprocity]** feature inherent in the term across both eras. Team Support posits that "relationship" has shifted from "being" to "doing," yet the OLD corpus already licenses the active maintenance and negotiation of status.

The strongest rebuttal lies in the OLD sentence: **"I think, ' said she, 'that the relationship existing between Harris and me, fully sanctions the intimacy of which you complain."**

In this instance, the "relationship" is not a static property of the universe, nor is it merely a blood-kinship tie. It is an active, negotiated state that "sanctions" (permits/authorizes) specific social behaviors. The speaker is actively invoking the "relationship" to define the boundaries of "intimacy." This proves that the **[+Agency/Negotiation]** feature identified in the modern corpus (e.g., "set boundaries... to determine what is acceptable") is not a new lexical sense, but a consistent application of the same core feature: the mutual, behavioral understanding between two parties.

The modern usage regarding "managing" or "solidifying" a relationship is simply a polysemous expansion of this existing feature. Whether in 1850 or 2010, a "relationship" functions as a reciprocal framework that dictates the acceptable conduct between participants. The shift is not in the *lexical sense* of the word, but in the *social context* of its application, confirming that "relationship" remains stable as a term for negotiated interpersonal connectivity.

### Rebuttal - Round 3

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Refuse’s weakest claim is that the modern focus on "managing" or "solidifying" a relationship is a mere polysemous expansion of the 19th-century usage, asserting that "relationship" has always functioned as a "negotiated framework" for conduct. 

This is directly contradicted by the OLD corpus sentence: **"They shall neither blush for nor lose by their relationship with Edward Clifford."** Here, "relationship" functions as an objective, binary status (likely familial or social standing) that is *possessed* or *lost* independently of the participants' agency. It is a state of being defined by external classification, not a project to be "solidified." Contrast this with the NEW corpus sentence: **"He would leave here more of a stranger than when he arrived, having been denied the chance to renew and solidify any of his relationships."** 

In the modern usage, the relationship is no longer a static fact of existence but a fragile, temporal entity that requires active, ongoing labor to maintain—if one fails to "solidify" it, the relationship effectively ceases to exist. Team Refuse misses the fundamental feature-level shift: the movement from **[+Status/Affiliation]** (an objective position within a social structure) to **[+Labor/Maintenance]** (a subjective, performative process). The 19th-century "relationship" was a noun of *being*; the 21st-century "relationship" is a noun of *process*. The "negotiation" Team Refuse cites in the OLD corpus is merely an appeal to an existing, pre-defined status, whereas the modern "setting of boundaries" is the *creation* of the relationship itself.

**Change Type:** Semantic Shift (from [+Status/Affiliation] to [+Labor/Maintenance]).
**Causal Driver:** Modernization of social structures, moving from fixed, hierarchical roles to fluid, performative interpersonal contracts.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Support’s strongest evidence is the contrast between the static "status" of the 19th century and the "labor-intensive" nature of modern relationships, specifically citing the sentence: **"He would leave here more of a stranger than when he arrived, having been denied the chance to renew and solidify any of his relationships."**

However, Team Support is mistaken to view "solidification" as a new lexical sense. The shared semantic feature that bridges OLD and NEW usage is **[+Mutual Engagement]**—the requirement of ongoing interaction to sustain the functional state of the connection. 

This feature is explicitly present in the OLD corpus sentence: **"I think, said she, that the relationship existing between Harris and me, fully sanctions the intimacy of which you complain."** 

In this 19th-century example, the "relationship" is not merely a passive, binary status (like a blood tie); it is a functional framework that "sanctions" (permits/authorizes) specific behaviors, such as "intimacy." The speaker acknowledges that the validity of this relationship depends on their shared conduct and the perception of that conduct by others. If the participants failed to engage in the "intimacy" or "companionable qualities" mentioned in other OLD sentences, the relationship would lose its functional power or social legitimacy. 

While the NEW corpus highlights "solidifying" or "setting boundaries," these are simply modern methods of navigating the same **[+Mutual Engagement]** that existed in 1810. The shift from "maintaining social propriety" to "maintaining personal intimacy" is a shift in the *domain* of application, not a change in the lexical sense of the word. The word continues to denote a state of interconnectedness that requires active maintenance to remain functional, proving that the semantic core remains stable across both centuries.

### Rebuttal - Round closing

#### 🔴 Team Support (Hypothesis: Change)

Team Support maintains that the evolution of "relationship" represents a fundamental semantic shift from a static descriptor of kinship or connection to an internal, psychological process.

Our strongest evidence lies in the shift from external social status to internal emotional investment. While the 1810–1860 corpus defines relationship through external standing—**"They shall neither blush for nor lose by their relationship with Edward Clifford"**—the modern corpus reflects a shift toward personal cultivation: **"He would leave here more of a stranger... having been denied the chance to renew and solidify any of his relationships."**

Team Refuse argues that the "labor" of maintenance proves stability, but they conflate social reputation with emotional process. The 1810–1860 sentence focuses on the *consequence* of a status, whereas the modern corpus focuses on the *internal experience* of "solidifying" a bond. Because the modern subject seeks to "renew" an internal connection rather than avoid "blushing" for a social one, the underlying semantic function has fundamentally diverged.

**Change Type:** Semantic Shift (External Status to Internal Process).
**Causal Driver:** Shift from social-reputational utility to psychological-relational maintenance.

#### 🟢 Team Refuse (Hypothesis: Stable)

Team Refuse maintains that the evolution of "relationship" is a matter of scope, not a fundamental rupture. 

Our strongest evidence for stability lies in the persistent requirement for external validation. In the 1810–1860 corpus, the sentence **"They shall neither blush for nor lose by their relationship with Edward Clifford"** demonstrates that a relationship is contingent upon the conduct of the participants; one can "lose" or compromise the status through action. This mirrors the modern corpus sentence: **"He would leave here more of a stranger... having been denied the chance to renew and solidify any of his relationships."**

Team Support argues that the modern usage represents a shift to a "noun of process," but this ignores that 19th-century subjects were already actively managing their standing. If the 1810–1860 relationship were merely an immutable "state of being," the participants could not "lose" it through their own behavior. By citing **"They shall neither blush for nor lose by their relationship,"** we demonstrate that the "labor" of maintenance has always been the mechanism by which the status is preserved, refuting the claim of a categorical semantic shift.

### ⚖️ LLM Judge

The debate demonstrates that the core semantic feature of 'relationship'—a dyadic or systemic link between entities that dictates the nature of their interaction—remains consistent across both corpora. Team Support argues for a shift from a 'static state' to a 'dynamic process' (labor/maintenance), but Team Refuse successfully counters this by showing that 19th-century usage already encompassed the active management of social bonds (e.g., 'sanctioning intimacy' or 'losing' a relationship through conduct). The observed differences in usage, such as the modern emphasis on 'setting boundaries' or 'solidifying' bonds, represent a change in the social domain and the cultural expectations of interpersonal engagement (register/topic shift) rather than a fundamental change in the lexical sense of the noun. Both periods utilize the word to describe a reciprocal framework that governs the behavior and status of the participants involved.
